For example, the postal code of \u003ccode\u003e245 SUMMER STREET\\nBOSTON MA 02210\u003c/code\u003e is \u003ccode\u003e2210\u003c/code\u003e. If it's in the form like \u003ccode\u003e53705-1234\u003c/code\u003e, only take \u003ccode\u003e53705\u003c/code\u003e. If it's neither 5 digits number nor 9 digits number, don't use the point.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eonly show the street with a postal code from 40000 to 70000\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003euse the \"magma\" colormap, with a colorbar\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ethe color of background is \"lightgray\"\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe result should look similar to this:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/blob/main/p5/geo.png\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/raw/main/p5/geo.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-conclusion\" class=\"anchor\" aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"#conclusion\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003eConclusion\u003c/h1\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe EDGAR logs are supposedly anonymized (with the last three docs\nleft), but we can still tell where the users live and what they're\nlooking at.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBy connecting the filing information with the logs, we can learn a lot about the behavior of the investment firms which use the database - for example, we might learn which companies (or industries) a hedge fund might be considering investing in, and the extent to which it relies on automated vs manual research in its trading.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOthers have used this same data to make good guesses\nabout what docs various hedge funds and others are looking at, then\ncorrelate that with success. cTsUqU js-snippet-clipboard-copy-unpositioned" data-hpc="true"><article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-p5-edgar-web-logs" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#p5-edgar-web-logs"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" <h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-correctionsclarifications" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#correctionsclarifications"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Corrections/Clarifications</h2>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>fixed incorrect 00 date (Yiyin, Apr 5). Please do a <code>git pull</code> to obtain the updated tester.</li>
</ul>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-overview" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#overview"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Overview</h2>
<p dir="auto">In the US, public companies need to regularly file
various statements and reports to the SEC's (Securities and Exchange
Commission) EDGAR database.  EDGAR data is publicly available online;
furthermore, web requests to EDGAR from around the world are logged
and published.  EDGAR logs are huge.  Logs for <em>just one day</em> might be
about 250 MB compressed as a .zip (or 2 GB uncompressed!).</p>
<p dir="auto">We'll develop tools to extract information from the filings stored in EDGAR (this will be done in a Python module, <code>edgar_utils.py</code>) and we'll use those tools to analyze user behavior in <code>p5.ipynb</code>.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-packages" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#packages"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Packages</h2>
<p dir="auto">You'll need to install some packages:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="pip3 install --upgrade pip
pip3 install geopandas shapely descartes geopy netaddr
sudo apt install -y python3-rtree"><pre class="notranslate"><code>pip3 install --upgrade pip
pip3 install geopandas shapely descartes geopy netaddr
sudo apt install -y python3-rtree
</code></pre></div>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-testing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#testing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Testing</h2>
<p dir="auto">Be sure to run <code>python3 tester.py</code> regularly to estimate your grade. As in Project 2, the tester will both check the results of the analysis in your notebook, and use <code>module_tester.py</code> to check your <code>edgar_utils.py</code> module.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-submission" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#submission"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Submission</h2>
<p dir="auto">As before, your notebook should have a comment like this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# project: p5
# submitter: ????
# partner: none
# hours: ????"><pre><span class="pl-c"># project: p5</span>
<span class="pl-c"># submitter: ????</span>
<span class="pl-c"># partner: none</span>
<span class="pl-c"># hours: ????</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">You'll hand in two files:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>p5.ipynb</code></li>
<li><code>edgar_utils.py</code></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Combine these into a zip by running the following in the <code>p5</code> directory:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="zip ../p5.zip p5.ipynb edgar_utils.py"><pre class="notranslate"><code>zip ../p5.zip p5.ipynb edgar_utils.py
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Hand in the resulting p5.zip file.  Don't zip a different way (our
tests won't run if you have an extra directory inside your zip, for
example).</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-format" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#data-format"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data format</h2>
<p dir="auto">Take a look at the list of daily zips and CSV documentation on the EDGAR site:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://www.sec.gov/dera/data/edgar-log-file-data-set.html" rel="nofollow">https://www.sec.gov/dera/data/edgar-log-file-data-set.html</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.sec.gov/files/EDGAR_variables_FINAL.pdf" rel="nofollow">https://www.sec.gov/files/EDGAR_variables_FINAL.pdf</a></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">We have provided a <code>server_log.zip</code> file, which is a subset of the
records from <code>log20170101.zip</code>. Since you'll need to work with a lot of zipped files for this project, you'll want to know some command line techniques
to troubleshoot.</p>
<p dir="auto">You could use <code>sudo apt install unzip</code> to install unzip, and then view names of files in a zip file:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="unzip -l server_log.zip"><pre class="notranslate"><code>unzip -l server_log.zip
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">View the start of a file inside of a zip file (change "head" to "tail"
to see the end):</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="unzip -p server_log.zip rows.csv | head -n 5"><pre class="notranslate"><code>unzip -p server_log.zip rows.csv | head -n 5
</code></pre></div>

<p dir="auto">Looking at the <code>cik</code>, <code>accession</code>, and <code>extention</code> fields tells you what web resoure a user was requesting (in particular, each company has it's own <code>cik</code>):</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="ip,date,time,zone,cik,accession,extention,code,size,idx,norefer,noagent,find,crawler,browser,region

</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">For this row, we can construct the following URL from <code>1461219.0</code>, <code>0001209191-21-001287</code>, and <code>-index.htm</code>:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1461219/0001209191-21-001287-index.htm" rel="nofollow">https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1461219/0001209191-21-001287-index.htm</a></p>
<p dir="auto">Looking at this page and its source (as well as the source of the pages where your parser does not behave as expected) is highly recommended and will be very important later in the project.</p>
<p dir="auto">We have already downloaded the docs for a subset of the requests in
<code>server_log.zip</code> for you and placed them in <code>docs.zip</code>. Note, however, that the file structure is slightly different than the URL above. The path in the zip to that file would be "1461219/0001209191-21-001287/-index.htm".</p>
<p dir="auto">Note that by default reading inside a zip gives you bytes.  For your regex work, convert to a string using UTF-8 (like we have done for <code>check_output</code>).</p>
<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-group-part-75" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#group-part-75"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Group Part (75%)</h1>
<p dir="auto">For this portion of the project, you may collaborate with your group
members in any way (even looking at working code).  You may also seek

seek receive help from other 320 students (outside your group) or

<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-1-server_logzip-analysis" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-1-server_logzip-analysis"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 1: <code>server_log.zip</code> analysis</h2>
<p dir="auto">Answer these questions in <code>p5.ipynb</code>.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q1-whats-the-total-size-in-bytes-of-the-files-requested" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q1-whats-the-total-size-in-bytes-of-the-files-requested"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q1: what's the total size in bytes of the files requested?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Look at the <code>size</code> column of the CSV in <code>server_log.zip</code>.  We want to
count duplicates here; this gives us an estimate of the amount of
network traffic handled by EDGAR (since this data is only a sample,
the true value will be even larger). Answer with an integer.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q2-how-many-filings-have-been-accessed-by-the-top-ten-ips" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q2-how-many-filings-have-been-accessed-by-the-top-ten-ips"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q2: how many filings have been accessed by the top ten IPs?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a dictionary, with the (anonymized) IP as key and the number of requests seen in the logs as the values. Each row in the logs corresponds to one request. Note that the anonymized IP addresses are consistent between requests.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Hint:</strong> for this question and most of the others expecting dictionary output, it might be easiest to use Pandas operations to process the data into a <code>Series</code> and to use the <code>to_dict()</code> method. Consider using tools like <code>groupby</code>, <code>apply</code>, and aggregation methods like <code>size()</code>. In Q30-32 from <a href="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/blob/main/p1/README.md">P1</a>, there is an example of <code>apply</code>.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q3-what-fraction-of-the-requests-had-errors" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q3-what-fraction-of-the-requests-had-errors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q3: what fraction of the requests had errors?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Count any request with a status code greater than or equal to 400 as having resulted in an error. Answer with a floating point number.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q4-what-is-the-most-frequently-accessed-file" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q4-what-is-the-most-frequently-accessed-file"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q4: what is the most frequently accessed file?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a string formatted like so: "cik/accession/extention" (these are the names of columns in "rows.csv").</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q5-how-many-requests-were-made-by-automated-crawlers" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q5-how-many-requests-were-made-by-automated-crawlers"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q5: how many requests were made by automated crawlers?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Only count the requests made by users who were identified as crawlers (see the crawler column); considering the results of Q2, this is likely to be a vast underestimate. Answer with an integer.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-2-creating-edgar_utilspy-module" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-2-creating-edgar_utilspy-module"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 2: creating <code>edgar_utils.py</code> module</h2>
<p dir="auto">This part is to be started during <a href="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/blob/main/labs/lab11.md">lab 10</a>.</p>

<p dir="auto">Finish the <code>edgar_utils.py</code> module now if you didn't have enough time
during the scheduled lab.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-3-using-edgar_utilspy-module" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-3-using-edgar_utilspy-module"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 3: using <code>edgar_utils.py</code> module</h2>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q6-which-region-uses-edgar-most-heavily" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q6-which-region-uses-edgar-most-heavily"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q6: which region uses EDGAR most heavily?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Use your <code>lookup_region</code> function and answer with a string.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q7-what-fraction-of-ips-in-each-region-are-high-volume-users" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q7-what-fraction-of-ips-in-each-region-are-high-volume-users"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q7: what fraction of IPs in each region are high-volume users?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Consider IPs which accessed more than 1000 EDGAR resoures to be
high-volume. This might indicate machines running automated scraping
and analysis tasks.</p>
<p dir="auto">Note that given the sampling done in the data, the true EDGAR usage of
these machines is likely to be even heavier.</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a dictionary, where the keys are the regions and the
values are the fraction (in floating point form) of IPs from that
region classified as high-volume.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example:</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">Say "United States of America" has four IPs:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>1.1.1.1 appears 1200 times in the logs</li>
<li>2.2.2.2 appears 900 times in the logs</li>
<li>3.3.3.3 appears 5 times in the logs</li>
<li>4.4.4.4 appears 234 times in the logs</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">This means that 1/4 of the IPs in the US are high volume, so there should be an entry like this:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="{
    &quot;United States of America&quot;: 0.25,
    ...
}"><pre class="notranslate"><code>{
    "United States of America": 0.25,
    ...
}
</code></pre></div>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q8-what-dates-appear-in-the-8506930000850693-07-000159-indexhtm-file-of-docszip" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q8-what-dates-appear-in-the-8506930000850693-07-000159-indexhtm-file-of-docszip"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q8: what dates appear in the <code>850693/0000850693-07-000159/-index.htm</code> file of <code>docs.zip</code>?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Read the HTML from this file and use it to create a <code>Filing</code> object,
from which you can access the <code>.dates</code> attribute.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Suggestion:</strong> read every .htm or .html file in <code>docs.zip</code>, creating a
<code>Filing</code> object from each.  Save the Filing objects in a dict, keyed
by filename, so you don't need to re-read the data for each of the
following questions.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q9-what-is-the-distribution-of-states-for-the-filings-in-docszip" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q9-what-is-the-distribution-of-states-for-the-filings-in-docszip"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q9: what is the distribution of states for the filings in <code>docs.zip</code>?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a dict, like the following:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="{'CA': 92,
 'NY': 83,
 'TX': 67,
 'MA': 30,
 'IL': 25,
 'PA': 25,
 'CO': 25,
 ...
}"><pre class="notranslate"><code>{'CA': 92,
 'NY': 83,
 'TX': 67,
 'MA': 30,
 'IL': 25,
 'PA': 25,
 'CO': 25,
 ...
}
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The showing order of each key-value pair doesn't really matter.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q10-what-is-the-distribution-of-sic-codes-for-the-filings-in-docszip" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q10-what-is-the-distribution-of-sic-codes-for-the-filings-in-docszip"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q10: what is the distribution of SIC codes for the filings in <code>docs.zip</code>?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer in the same format as in the previous question.  This time,
skip any <code>None</code> values (<code>None</code> shouldn't be a key in the final dict).</p>
<p dir="auto">If you're curious, consider looking up the industry names for the top
couple categories:
<a href="https://www.sec.gov/corpfin/division-of-corporation-finance-standard-industrial-classification-sic-code-list" rel="nofollow">https://www.sec.gov/corpfin/division-of-corporation-finance-standard-industrial-classification-sic-code-list</a></p>
<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-individual-part-25" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#individual-part-25"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Individual Part (25%)</h1>
<p dir="auto">You have to do the remainder of this project on your own.  Do not
discuss with anybody except 320 staff (mentors, TAs, instructor).</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-4-combining-logs-with-documents" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-4-combining-logs-with-documents"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 4: combining logs with documents</h2>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q11-what-is-the-distribution-of-requests-across-industries" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q11-what-is-the-distribution-of-requests-across-industries"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q11: what is the distribution of requests across industries?</h3>
<p dir="auto">For each request in the logs that has a corresponding filing in
<code>docs.zip</code>, lookup the SIC (ignore rows in the logs which refer to
pages not in <code>docs.zip</code>).</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a dictionary, where the keys are the SIC and the values
are the number of times the resources of that industry were accessed.</p>
<p dir="auto">Expected output:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="{2834: 984,
 1389: 656,
 1311: 550,
 2836: 429,
 6022: 379,
 1000: 273,
 ...
 }"><pre class="notranslate"><code>{2834: 984,
 1389: 656,
 1311: 550,
 2836: 429,
 6022: 379,
 1000: 273,
 ...
 }
</code></pre></div>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q12-how-many-requests-were-made-in-each-hour" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q12-how-many-requests-were-made-in-each-hour"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q12: how many requests were made in each hour?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Use <code>pd.to_datetime</code> (the <code>hour</code> attributes of the converted
timestamps may be useful) or string manipulation to process the <code>time</code>
column. Answer with a dictionary, where the keys are integers from 0
to 23 representing the hour of the day, and the values are the number
of requests made in that hour.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q13-what-is-the-geographic-overlap-in-interest-between-australia-france-and-viet-nam" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q13-what-is-the-geographic-overlap-in-interest-between-australia-france-and-viet-nam"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q13: what is the geographic overlap in interest between Australia, France, and Viet Nam?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a Digraph like the following:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/blob/main/p5/digraph.png"><img src="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/raw/main/p5/digraph.png" width="400" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">In addition to a node for each of these three countries, there should
be a node for each state having a filing accessed by somebody in one
of these countries.</p>
<p dir="auto">An edge from a country to a state means somebody in that country
looked at least one filing for a company in that state.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q14-what-are-the-most-commonly-seen-street-addresses" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q14-what-are-the-most-commonly-seen-street-addresses"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q14: what are the most commonly seen street addresses?</h3>
<p dir="auto">For each web request that has a corresponding filing, count each of
the addresses for that filing.</p>
<p dir="auto">Show a dictionary of counts for all addresses appearing at least 225
times.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q15-geographic-plotting-of-postal-code" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q15-geographic-plotting-of-postal-code"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q15: geographic plotting of postal code</h3>
<p dir="auto">The <code>locations.geojson</code> contains the positions of some of the
addresses in the dataset.  Plot this over the background map in
"shapes/cb_2018_us_state_20m.shp"</p>
<p dir="auto">Additional requirements:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>crop to the following lat/lon bounds:</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="west = -90
east = -55
north = 50
south = 35"><pre><span class="pl-s1">west</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">-</span><span class="pl-c1">90</span>
<span class="pl-s1">east</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">-</span><span class="pl-c1">55</span>
<span class="pl-s1">north</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">50</span>
<span class="pl-s1">south</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">35</span></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>use a Mercator projection, "epsg:2022"</li>
<li>the color of each point should indicate the postal code. For example, the postal code of <code>245 SUMMER STREET\nBOSTON MA 02210</code> is <code>2210</code>. If it's in the form like <code>53705-1234</code>, only take <code>53705</code>. If it's neither 5 digits number nor 9 digits number, don't use the point.</li>
<li>only show the street with a postal code from 40000 to 70000</li>
<li>use the "magma" colormap, with a colorbar</li>
<li>the color of background is "lightgray"</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">The result should look similar to this:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/blob/main/p5/geo.png"><img src="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/raw/main/p5/geo.png" alt="" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-conclusion" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#conclusion"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Conclusion</h1>
<p dir="auto">The EDGAR logs are supposedly anonymized (with the last three docs
left), but we can still tell where the users live and what they're
looking at.</p>
<p dir="auto">By connecting the filing information with the logs, we can learn a lot about the behavior of the investment firms which use the database - for example, we might learn which companies (or industries) a hedge fund might be considering investing in, and the extent to which it relies on automated vs manual research in its trading.</p>
<p dir="auto">Others have used this same data to make good guesses
about what docs various hedge funds and others are looking at, then
correlate that with success.  For those interested in the nitty-gritty
details of what could be done with this data, take a look at this
early-stage work: <a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3127825" rel="nofollow">Hedge Funds and Public Information
Acquisition</a>.</p>
